10134{_}731{_}This group went off by itself into a remote part of the church.
10134{_}732{_}It furnished no substitute teachers.
10134{_}733{_}It wasn't heard of at all.
10134{_}734{_}And loud were the complaints about its crippling the school.
10134{_}735{_}"But, pastor, you should have seen the difference when the first dozen real teachers came out of that class; we were able to reorganize the whole school.
10134{_}736{_}Our John Wesley got a teacher he'll never forget.
10134{_}737{_}And, of course, we kept the training class going; it's never stopped since.
10134{_}738{_}The Board of Sunday Schools has given us the courses and helped us keep the class up to grade in its work, and you know what sort of teachers we have now."
10134{_}739{_}The pastor did, and was properly thankful.
10134{_}740{_}In some of his other pastorates it had been otherwise, to his sorrow.
10134{_}741{_}"Speaking of the Board of Sunday Schools," the elder Farwell resumed, for this was a hobby he missed no chance to ride, "it made all the difference with us in our work for a better Sunday school--gave us expert backing, you know.
10134{_}742{_}And I notice by its latest annual report--yes, I always get a copy, though J.W.
10134{_}743{_}thinks it dry reading--that it is helping Sunday schools by the thousand, not in this country only, but wherever in the world our church is at work.
10134{_}744{_}Of course you know how it starts Sunday schools, and how often they grow into churches.
10134{_}745{_}Well, it didn't quite do that here, but this church is a sight better and bigger because we began to take the Board's advice when we did.
10134{_}746{_}It was a good thing for our boy, and many another boy and girl, that the Board woke us up."
10134{_}747{_}"It hasn't all been easy work, though," the minister suggested.
10134{_}748{_}"I remember that when I came I found there was a good deal of discontent over the Graded Lessons."
10134{_}749{_}"Sure there was," said J.W., Sr. "We had all been brought up on the Uniform Lessons, and most of us thought they were just right.
10134{_}750{_}Besides, we rather enjoyed thinking of ourselves as keeping step with the whole Sunday school world--all over the wide earth everybody studying the same scripture on the same Sunday.
10134{_}751{_}And that was a big idea to get into the minds of Christians of every name everywhere."
10134{_}752{_}"Yes, but, Dad," put in J.W., "what was the good of it if the lessons didn't fit everybody?
10134{_}753{_}Did people think that the kids in the primary and their mothers in ma's class ought to study the same lesson?
10134{_}754{_}or did they think they could fit the same lesson to everybody by the different notes they put into the Quarterlies?"
10134{_}755{_}"Well, son," his father replied, "I reckon we thought both ways.
10134{_}756{_}And I'm not so sure yet that it can't be done.
10134{_}757{_}But if one thing more than another reconciled me to the Graded Lessons, it was that they made being a Sunday school teacher a good deal bigger job than it had ever been.
10134{_}758{_}It was harder work, because every lesson had to be studied by the teacher, and in a different way from what was thought good enough in the old days.
10134{_}759{_}And I'm for anything, Graded Lessons or whatever, that'll make people take Sunday school teaching more seriously."
10134{_}760{_}Then Mrs. Farwell ventured to take up the story.
10134{_}761{_}It was about that time, in the very beginning of the Drury pastorate, that J.W.
10134{_}762{_}joined the church on probation; much to her surprise and humbling.
10134{_}763{_}"I hadn't even thought of it," she said, "though I should have been the first one.
10134{_}764{_}He had been getting ready in the Junior League, as I very well knew, but one day, as you may remember"--Brother Drury did, for that day was the real beginning of this story--"you made an invitation at the end of a real simple sermon, and if J.W., Jr., didn't get right up from my side and walk straight to the front!"
10134{_}765{_}After that there had been a probationers' class, with J.W.
10134{_}766{_}and perhaps twenty others meeting the pastor every week for straight religious teaching, so that at Easter, when they came up for membership, what with their Sunday school and Junior League training, and what with the pastor's more personal instruction, they were able to pass a pretty fair examination on the great Christian truths, and on the general scheme of the church's work.
10134{_}767{_}"For a time mother was a trifle disappointed that J.W.
10134{_}768{_}hadn't waited for the big revival we had the next year," said J.W., Sr., "but I think she was glad afterward."
10134{_}769{_}"Yes, I was," the mother said.
10134{_}770{_}"You see, I had been brought up to believe in revivals, and I do yet, but we had no such chance to get the right Christian start when we were little children, as J.W.
10134{_}771{_}has had, if you'll let his mother say so, and that made a revival a good deal more important to us when our church did get ready for one.
10134{_}772{_}But the other way is all right too.
10134{_}773{_}I'm mother enough to be glad J.W.
10134{_}774{_}hasn't known some of the experiences the boys of my time went through, and the girls as well.
10134{_}775{_}He's no worse a Christian for having been right in the church ever since I put him in short dresses, are you, son?
10134{_}776{_}And I will say that his father was always with me in holding to the promises we made when he was baptized.
10134{_}777{_}We've not done what we might, but we've never forgotten that those promises were made to be kept."
10134{_}778{_}J.W.
10134{_}779{_}felt none of his old shrinking from such talk, especially since the Institute, and yet he had the healthy boy's reluctance to discuss himself in company.
10134{_}780{_}But this was interesting him, outside himself.
10134{_}781{_}He turned to the pastor.
10134{_}782{_}"That's what I meant when I told you what Phil said.
10134{_}783{_}I'm all for the church, and church people and church ways; why shouldn't I be?
10134{_}784{_}I've never known anything else.
10134{_}785{_}I remember well the one thing I didn't like when it first came along; and that was the new sort of Christmas celebration Dad and the others planned when I was ten or eleven.
10134{_}786{_}You know what Christmas means to such kids, and I guess we were all selfish together, because we didn't use our heads.
10134{_}787{_}Well, the Sunday school proposed that instead of us all getting something we should all give something.
10134{_}788{_}It looked pretty cheap to us little fellows at first, and our teacher had all he could do to hold us in line.
10134{_}789{_}But let me tell you, every boy was for it when the time came.
10134{_}790{_}We found that we could have as much fun giving things away as we could grabbing things, and, anyway, nobody really cared for those mosquito net stockings filled with nuts and candy and one orange.
10134{_}791{_}It was only the idea of getting something for nothing.
10134{_}792{_}That first 'giving Christmas,' I remember, our class dressed up as delivery boys, and we came on the platform with enough groceries for a small truck load, that we had bought with our own money.
10134{_}793{_}The orphanage got 'em next day.
10134{_}794{_}And one class was dusty millers, carrying sacks of flour, and another put on a stunt of searching for Captain Kidd's treasure, and they found a keg of shining coins (new pennies, they were)--more than a thousand of 'em.
10134{_}795{_}Everything went to the orphanage, or the hospital; and then when the Board of Sunday Schools began to get us interested in other Sunday schools and in missions--I remember a scheme they call a 'Partnership Plan' that was great; I don't know what happened to it--I got right into the game every time."
10134{_}796{_}"How do you happen to know so much about the Board of Sunday Schools, J.W.?"
10134{_}797{_}asked Mr. Drury.
10134{_}798{_}"Oh, that's easy.
10134{_}799{_}You know how it is in our Sunday school: they don't make one or two of us young fellows serve as librarians and secretaries and such and miss all the class work: they have more help, and we all get into class for the lesson.
10134{_}800{_}Well, two years ago Dad told me you had nominated me for something at the annual Sunday school meeting.
10134{_}801{_}It was only a sort of assistant secretary's job, but very soon I began to catch on, and I've seen a lot of the letters and leaflets that come from the Board in Chicago.
10134{_}802{_}Well, let me tell you that Board of Sunday Schools is a whale of a machine.
10134{_}803{_}Why, it's the whole church at work to make better Sunday schools, and more of 'em.
10134{_}804{_}They have Sunday school workers in all sorts of wild places, and Sunday school missionaries in foreign lands.
10134{_}805{_}Yes, and last year I happened to meet one of their secretaries, at your house, you may remember.
10134{_}806{_}But you'd never think he was just a secretary, he was so keen and wide awake.
10134{_}807{_}He knew the Boy Scouts from A to Z, and that got me, 'cause I'm not so old that I've forgotten my scouting.
10134{_}808{_}And he knew baseball, and boys' books, and all that.
10134{_}809{_}Don't you think, Brother Drury, if more of the fellows knew what the real Sunday school work is they would take to it like colts to a bran mash?"
10134{_}810{_}"They couldn't help it," said the pastor.
10134{_}811{_}"And you may have noticed that your father and the other people of our Sunday School Board are trying to get them to find out some of the things you have found out.
10134{_}812{_}For instance, you know what the two organized classes of high-school freshmen are doing, and the other organized classes.
10134{_}813{_}Seems to me their members are finding out that Sunday school is something big and fine."
10134{_}814{_}"That they are," Mrs. Farwell agreed, "and you mustn't forget my wonderful class of young married women, and the men's class of nearly a hundred.
10134{_}815{_}I think our Sunday school has really begun to change the ideas of a lot of people.
10134{_}816{_}Just think how little trouble we have now with what Graded Lessons we have, and how happy all our teachers are because they have the helps they need for just the sort of pupils that are in their classes."
10134{_}817{_}"That's so," said J.W., Sr. "I don't suppose even old Brother Barnacle, 'sot' as he is, would vote to go back to the times when the superintendent reviewed the lesson the same way the teachers taught it, from a printed list of questions.
10134{_}818{_}Seems as if I can hear Henry J. Locke yet--his farm joins ours down by the creek--when he conducted the reviewing at Deep Creek.
10134{_}819{_}He would hold his quarterly at arm's length to favor his eyes, and then look up from it to the school and shoot the question at everybody, 'And what did Peter do _then_, HEY?'
10134{_}820{_}He sure did come out strong on Peter; but I'll say this for him, that he never skipped a question from start to finish."
10134{_}821{_}All three laughed a little over Henry J. Locke, and then the pastor said he mustn't stay much longer.
10134{_}822{_}But he did want to back up J.W.
10134{_}823{_}'s belief that what Phil Khamis had said was true of everybody--we are all debtors.
10134{_}824{_}"Look at this young J.W.
10134{_}825{_}here, will you," he said to the father and mother, for once letting himself go, "with a name he's proud of, and a home life that many a Fifth Avenue and Lake Shore Drive family would be glad to pay a million for, if such goods were on sale in the stores.
10134{_}826{_}I'm going to tell him something he already knows.
10134{_}827{_}Young man," and there was a gleam in the pastor's eye that was not all to the credit of the work he was praising, "you owe a big debt to the Sunday school.
10134{_}828{_}I'm not jealous for the church, or for any other part of it, but by your own admission the Sunday school has had a lot to do with your education.
10134{_}829{_}Very well; remember it is a part of what Phil said, and what you are because of the Sunday school you have become by the goodness of Christian people.
10134{_}830{_}I don't think you'll forget it, seeing that you have two of that sort of people in your own home all the time."
10134{_}831{_}And then, with a fine naturalness the little group knelt by the chairs, and two of the four, he who was pastor of the whole flock and he who with simple dignity was priest in his own household, gave thanks to God for the manifold goodness of Christian people, of which they were all partakers every day.
10134{_}832{_}As he went home, Walter Drury thought of the long days that stretched out ahead before he could see the outcomes of the great Experiment, but this night had seen a good night's work done in the laboratory, and he was content.
10134{_}833{_}One tale of the past had been much in J.W.
10134{_}834{_}'s thought that night, but nothing on earth could have induced him to talk about it, especially since the happenings at the Institute.
10134{_}835{_}Only one other person knew all of its inwardness, though the preacher guessed most of the secret pretty shrewdly, and everybody was familiar with its outcome.
10134{_}836{_}It was the story of Marty Shenk's conversion.
10134{_}837{_}These two had been David and Jonathan from their little boy days, no less friends because they were so unlike; Marty, a quiet, brooding, knowledge-hungry youngster, and J.W.
10134{_}838{_}matter-of-fact, taking things as they came and asking few questions, but always the leader in games and mischief; each the other's champion against all comers.
10134{_}839{_}Marty's father, tenant-farmer on the Farwell farm, was steady enough and dependable, but never one to get ahead much.
10134{_}840{_}Before the Farwells moved to town he had rarely stayed on the same farm more than a year or two, but, as he said, "J.W.
10134{_}841{_}Farwell was different, and anybody who wanted to be decent could get along with him."
10134{_}842{_}So, for many Saturdays and vacations of boyhood years J.W.
10134{_}843{_}and Marty had roamed the countryside, and were letter-perfect in their boy-knowledge of the old farm.
10134{_}844{_}Marty came in to high school from the farm, and often he stayed with J.W.
10134{_}845{_}over the weekend.
10134{_}846{_}His school work was uneven--ahead in mathematics, and the sciences, and something below the average in other studies.
10134{_}847{_}That, however, has no place in this story.
10134{_}848{_}Of course he and J.W.
10134{_}849{_}were thick as thieves.
10134{_}850{_}Except when class work made temporary separations necessary, they lived the high-school life together.
10134{_}851{_}That meant also, for these two, the social life of the church, which occasionally paid special attention to the students.
10134{_}852{_}So you might find them at Epworth League socials, Sunday school class doings, in the Sunday school orchestra--violin and b-flat cornet respectively--and, most significant of all in its effect on all the later years, they went through Win-My-Chum week together.
10134{_}853{_}The hand of the pastor was in that, too.
10134{_}854{_}Marty was not a Christian.
10134{_}855{_}J.W.
10134{_}856{_}had been a church member for years, and early in his course he had faced and accepted all that being a Christian seemed to mean to a high-school boy.
10134{_}857{_}There had been hard places to get over; some of the boys and girls were merciless in their unconscious tests of his religion.
10134{_}858{_}Some were openly scornful, and others sought by indirect and furtive means to break his influence in the school.
10134{_}859{_}For he had no small gift of leadership, and he cared a good deal that it should count for the decencies of high-school life.
10134{_}860{_}By senior year the sort of trouble that a Christian boy encounters in school was almost all ended, but it had been more through his dogged resistance to opposition than because of any special zest in Christian service.
10134{_}861{_}And then came the announcement of Win-My-Chum week, with J.W.
10134{_}862{_}confronted by two stubborn facts.
10134{_}863{_}He had only one real chum, and that chum was not a Christian.
10134{_}864{_}Pastor Drury had let fall a remark, a month before the Week, to the effect that any Christian who had a chum could dodge Win-My-Chum week, but he couldn't dodge his chum.
10134{_}865{_}When the week was past, the chum would still be on hand.
10134{_}866{_}Think as he would, there was no honest way of escape from whatever those facts might require of him, so J.W., long accustomed to go ahead and take what came, had known himself bound by the obligations of this matter also, days and days before the activities of Win-My-Chum week began.
10134{_}867{_}The two were out one Saturday on the north road.
10134{_}868{_}They had been up to the woods on Barker's Hill for nuts, and with good success.
10134{_}869{_}The day was warm, the way was long, and there was no hurry.
10134{_}870{_}When they came to the roadside at the wood's edge they sat on a fallen tree and talked.
10134{_}871{_}At least Marty did.
10134{_}872{_}For J.W.
10134{_}873{_}was not himself.
10134{_}874{_}It was his chance, and he knew it.
10134{_}875{_}But a thousand impulses leaped to life within him to make him put off what he knew he ought to say.
10134{_}876{_}The fear of being misunderstood--even by Marty--the knowledge that Marty, in the qualities by which boys judge and are judged, was quite as "good" as himself; and, above all, his sense of total unfitness to be a pattern of the Christian life to anybody, filled him with an uneasiness that actually hurt.
10134{_}877{_}And Marty soon discovered that something was amiss.
10134{_}878{_}Willing as he was to do his full share of the talking, he became aware that except for inarticulate commonplaces he was having to do it all.
10134{_}879{_}"What's the matter with you all at once, J.W.?"
10134{_}880{_}he asked.
10134{_}881{_}"You're not taken suddenly sick, are you?
10134{_}882{_}You were all right when we were among the trees.
10134{_}883{_}_Are_ you sick?"
10134{_}884{_}J.W.
10134{_}885{_}laughed shortly.
10134{_}886{_}"No, old man, I'm not sick.
10134{_}887{_}But I'm up against a new game, for me, and I'm not in training."
10134{_}888{_}"Sounds interesting," said Marty, "but sort of mysterious.
10134{_}889{_}Is it anything I can do team-work on?"
10134{_}890{_}"It surely is, but first I've got to say something, and I want you to promise that you won't think I'm putting on, or butting in, because I'm not; nothing like it.
10134{_}891{_}Will you?"
10134{_}892{_}"Will I promise?"
10134{_}893{_}said Marty, much bewildered.
10134{_}894{_}"Course I'll promise not to think anything about you that you don't want me to think, but I must say I don't know within a thousand miles what you're driving at.
10134{_}895{_}Out with it, and even if you're the train bandit who held up the Cannonball or if you've plotted to kidnap the Board of Education, I'll never tell."
10134{_}896{_}Marty's quizzical humor was not making J.W.
10134{_}897{_}'s enterprise any easier.
10134{_}898{_}He had always supposed that what the leaflets called "personal evangelism" had to be done in a spirit of solemnity.
10134{_}899{_}But how was he to acquire the proper frame of mind?
10134{_}900{_}And certainly there was nothing solemn about Marty just now.
10134{_}901{_}Yet the thing had gone too far; it was too late to retreat.
10134{_}902{_}He tried to think how Mr. Drury would do it, but saw only that if it was Mr.
10134{_}903{_}Dairy's business he would go straight to the center of it.
10134{_}904{_}Desperately, therefore, he plunged in.
10134{_}905{_}"Well, Marty," he said, speaking now with nervous haste, "what I'm up against is this.
10134{_}906{_}What's the matter with your being a Christian?"
10134{_}907{_}He will never forget the swift look of blank amazement that Marty turned on him, nor the slow-mounting flush that followed the first astonished start.
10134{_}908{_}For Marty did not answer, and turned his face away.
10134{_}909{_}J.W.
10134{_}910{_}was sure that in his blundering bluntness he had offended and probably angered his closest friend.
10134{_}911{_}The distress of that thought served at least to drive away all the self-consciousness which thus far had plagued him.
10134{_}912{_}"Say, Marty," he pleaded, putting his hand on the other's arm, "forget it, if I've hurt your feelings.
10134{_}913{_}I know as well as you do that I'm not fit to talk about such things to anybody, and, honest, I meant nothing but to say what I knew I'd got to say."
10134{_}914{_}Then Marty turned himself back slowly, and J.W.
10134{_}915{_}saw the troubled look in his eyes.
10134{_}916{_}In a voice that trembled despite his proud effort at control, he said, "Old man, you needn't apologize.
10134{_}917{_}You did surprise me, I'll admit; I wasn't looking for anything like this.
10134{_}918{_}It's all right, though, and I'm certainly not mad about it.
10134{_}919{_}But, say, J.W., let me put something up to you.
10134{_}920{_}Why did you never think to ask me that question before?"
10134{_}921{_}"Why, it was this way," J.W.
10134{_}922{_}began, somewhat puzzled at the form of the question, and still thinking he must set himself right with Marty.
10134{_}923{_}"You know the Epworth League is planning for those special meetings soon--'Win-My-Chum Week'--and I've been asked to lead one of the meetings.
10134{_}924{_}But you can see that I wouldn't be ready to lead a meeting like that unless I had put this thing of being a Christian up to you, anyway.
10134{_}925{_}You're the only real chum I've got.
10134{_}926{_}Mr. Drury said something a little while ago that made it mighty plain."
10134{_}927{_}"Yes," said Marty, "I can see that.
10134{_}928{_}But why did you never say anything to me about it when there wasn't any meeting coming?
10134{_}929{_}Haven't we always shared everything else, since away back?
10134{_}930{_}This is the one subject that you and I have kept away from in our talk of all we've ever thought about, and I was wondering why."
10134{_}931{_}"Well, I don't exactly know," J.W.
10134{_}932{_}replied.
10134{_}933{_}"It may have been that it never seemed to be any of my business; that it was the preacher's business, or the Sunday school teacher's, or somebody's.
10134{_}934{_}And you know I've always been surer of what you really are than I have of myself.
10134{_}935{_}I think I was always afraid you would either make fun of me or believe I was letting on to be better than you were.
10134{_}936{_}But when the League got into this Win-My-Chum plan, why, the name itself was an eye-opener.
10134{_}937{_}And I've seen lately that a fellow's got to be a Christian, out and out, or his religion is no good.
10134{_}938{_}And when I heard the preacher say, not long ago, that a fellow might dodge Win-My-Chum week, but he couldn't forever dodge his chum, I knew I had to speak to you.
10134{_}939{_}But you're sure you're not offended?"
10134{_}940{_}"Let me admit a thing to you, J.W.
10134{_}941{_}I've never said so before, but I've been wanting somebody to ask me to be a Christian for a long time.
10134{_}942{_}I was a coward about it, and wouldn't let on.
10134{_}943{_}I've been wanting to find out what I've got to do, but I wouldn't ask.
10134{_}944{_}Do you think I _could_ be a Christian?"
10134{_}945{_}"I know you could be a long way better Christian than I am," J.W.
10134{_}946{_}answered with unwonted feeling.
10134{_}947{_}"And if you did take Jesus Christ to be your Master, it would be more than just your getting religion.
10134{_}948{_}You would be the biggest kind of stand-by for me and for other people I know of.
10134{_}949{_}It's the one thing you need to be a hundred per cent right.
10134{_}950{_}I'm a pretty poor Christian, myself, Marty, partly because I don't know how to think much about it, but you'd be dead in earnest to get all that there is in the Christian life, and maybe I could follow along behind.
10134{_}951{_}You've always helped every other way, and I've always wanted you to help me be a genuine Christian."
10134{_}952{_}Marty put his hand on J.W.
10134{_}953{_}'s shoulder and looked him straight in the eye: "You've got me rated a lot too high," he said.
10134{_}954{_}"How can I help you?
10134{_}955{_}But we two have been pretty good chums so far, haven't we?
10134{_}956{_}Well, there's a lot to settle before I can be sure I'm a Christian, but it means everything for you to think I can be of some use.
10134{_}957{_}And I promise you this, J.W., I'll not let up until I am a Christian, and we'll stick together all the more, when I am, us two.
10134{_}958{_}Is that ago?"
10134{_}959{_}It was a go.
10134{_}960{_}J.W.
10134{_}961{_}was ready and far more than ready to call it a go.
10134{_}962{_}It had been easier than he had expected, but then it had all been so different from the vague and formal thing he had been afraid of.
10134{_}963{_}He could hardly believe, but he had one request to make.
10134{_}964{_}"I know you'll settle whatever has to be settled," he said, a bit unsteadily, "but when it's all done, and you tell people about it, as I know you will, please, Marty, don't bring me into it.
10134{_}965{_}Publicly, I mean.
10134{_}966{_}Let's just have this understanding between ourselves.
10134{_}967{_}I can lead my meeting now, but there's no need to say anything about me.
10134{_}968{_}Besides, I made a mess of it."
10134{_}969{_}"It may be the best mess anybody ever stirred up for me, J.W., but I won't say anything to worry you, if the time comes for me to say anything at all.
10134{_}970{_}And I believe it will."
10134{_}971{_}It did.
10134{_}972{_}Marty and the pastor had two or three long interviews.
10134{_}973{_}From the last of them the boy came away with a new light on his face and a new spring in his step.
10134{_}974{_}Evidently whatever needed to be settled, had been settled.
10134{_}975{_}He kept his promise to his chum, but that did not prevent him from choosing the night when J.W.
10134{_}976{_}led the meeting to stand up at the first opportunity and make his straightforward confession of love and loyalty, since God had made him a sharer in the life that is in Christ.
10134{_}977{_}Then for a moment J.W.
10134{_}978{_}feared Marty might forget their agreement, but Marty said simply, "And part of the joy that is in my heart to-night is because there is a new tie, the only other one we needed, between myself and my old-time chum, the leader of this meeting."
10134{_}979{_}In the back of the room Walter Drury, quietly looking on, sent up a silent thanksgiving.
10134{_}980{_}The great Experiment was going well.
10134{_}981{_}CHAPTER III   CAMPUS DAYS  So it was that J.W.
10134{_}982{_}and Marty had come into the inner places of each other's lives.
10134{_}983{_}Of all the developments of Institute week, naturally the one which filled J.W.
10134{_}984{_}'s thoughts with a sort of awed gladness was Marty's decision to offer himself for the ministry.
10134{_}985{_}Joe Carbrook's right-about-face was much more dramatic, for J.W.
10134{_}986{_}saw, when the decision was made, that Marty could not have been meant for anything but a preacher.
10134{_}987{_}It was as fit as you please.
10134{_}988{_}As to Joe, previous opinion had been pretty equally divided; one side leaning to the idea that he might make a lawyer, and the other predicting that he was more likely to be a perpetual and profitable client for some other lawyer.
10134{_}989{_}In the light of the Institute happenings, it was to be expected that the question of college would promptly become a practical matter to four Delafield people.
10134{_}990{_}Marty was greatly troubled, for he knew if he was to be a preacher, he must go to college, and he couldn't see how.
10134{_}991{_}J.W.
10134{_}992{_}felt no great urge, though it had always been understood that he would go.
10134{_}993{_}Marcia Dayne had one year of normal school to her credit, and would take another next year, perhaps; but this year she must teach.
10134{_}994{_}Joe Carbrook spent little time in debate with himself; he let everybody know that he was going to be a missionary doctor, and that he would go to the State University for the rest of his college course.
10134{_}995{_}"But what about the religious influence of the University?"
10134{_}996{_}Marcia Dayne had ventured to ask him one evening as they walked slowly under the elms of Monroe Avenue.
10134{_}997{_}"I don't know about that," Joe answered, "and maybe I'm making a mistake.
10134{_}998{_}But I don't think so.
10134{_}999{_}To begin with, there isn't any question about equipment at the State University.
10134{_}1000{_}They have everything any church school has, and probably more than most church schools, for what I want.
10134{_}1001{_}And they work in close relationship to the medical school.
10134{_}1002{_}That's one thing.
10134{_}1003{_}The big reason, though--I wonder if you'll understand it?"
10134{_}1004{_}"I believe I could understand anything you might be thinking about--now, Joe."
10134{_}1005{_}And Marcia's voice had in it a note which stirred that usually self-possessed young man out of all his easy composure.
10134{_}1006{_}"I'll remember that, Marcia," he said in the thrill of a swift elation.
10134{_}1007{_}"I'll remember that, because I think you do--understand, and some day I--but I've got at least five years of plugging ahead of me, and----"  "You were going to tell me about your big reason for going to the State University," Marcia broke in, though she wondered afterward if her instinct had not played her false.
10134{_}1008{_}"Yes," Joe said, with a little effort.
10134{_}1009{_}"Well, this is it.
10134{_}1010{_}You know I didn't make much of a hit at college; I pulled through sophomore year, but that's about all, and I doubt if the faculty will pass resolutions of regret when I don't show up there in the fall.
10134{_}1011{_}The religious influences of a church school didn't prevent me from being a good deal of a heathen, though I will say that was no fault of the school.
10134{_}1012{_}Maybe I ought to go back and face the music.
10134{_}1013{_}It wouldn't be so bad, I guess.
10134{_}1014{_}But I feel more like making a clean, new start, in a new place.
10134{_}1015{_}The State University wouldn't be any worse for me than I should be for it, if nothing had happened to change my point of view.
10134{_}1016{_}So, that isn't the issue.
10134{_}1017{_}But if the State University life is able to beat me before I get to sawing bones at all, I'd make a pretty missionary doctor if I ever landed in foreign parts, wouldn't I?"
10134{_}1018{_}Marcia could find nothing to say; perhaps because her thoughts were busy with other and more personal aspects of Joe's plans for the future.
10134{_}1019{_}And as Joe's people were completely oblivious to everything except the startling change that had come over him, and were abundantly able to send him to three universities at once if necessary, Joe Carbrook was as good as enrolled.
10134{_}1020{_}Marty and J.W.
10134{_}1021{_}did not find the future opening up before them so easily.
10134{_}1022{_}Marty, for all he could not imagine the way opening before such as himself, was all eagerness about the nearest Methodist school, which happened to be the one where the Institute had been held, Cartwright College.
10134{_}1023{_}It was named, as may be supposed, in honor of Peter Cartwright, that pioneer Methodist preacher who became famous on the same sort of schooling which sufficed for Abraham Lincoln, and once ran against Lincoln himself for Congress.
10134{_}1024{_}J.W.
10134{_}1025{_}was not specially eager to look for a college education anywhere.
10134{_}1026{_}Why should he be, since he was expecting to go into business?
10134{_}1027{_}The two had many a discussion, Marty arguing in favor of college for everybody, and J.W.
10134{_}1028{_}admitting that for preachers and teachers and lawyers and doctors it was necessary, but what use could it be in business?
10134{_}1029{_}"But say, J.W., you're not going to be one of these 'born a man, died a grocer' sort of business men," urged Marty.
10134{_}1030{_}"Broad-minded--that's your future, with a knowledge of more than markets.
10134{_}1031{_}And look at the personal side of college life.
10134{_}1032{_}Haven't you heard Mr. Drury say that if he hadn't anything else to show for his four years at college than the lifelong friendships he made there it would have been worth all it cost?
10134{_}1033{_}And you have reason to know he doesn't forget the studies."
10134{_}1034{_}"That's all right, Marty," J.W.
10134{_}1035{_}rejoined.
10134{_}1036{_}"I don't need much convincing on that score.
10134{_}1037{_}I can see the good times too; you know I'd try for all the athletics I could get into, and I guess I could keep my end up socially.
10134{_}1038{_}But is all that worth my time for the next four years, studying subjects that would be no earthly good to me in business, in making a living, I mean?
10134{_}1039{_}The other boys in hardware stores would have four years the start of me."
10134{_}1040{_}"But don't you remember, J.W., what our commencement speaker said on that very point?
10134{_}1041{_}He told us we had to be men and women first, no matter what occupations we got into.
10134{_}1042{_}And he bore down hard on how it was a good deal bigger business to make a life than to make a living.
10134{_}1043{_}In these days the most dangerous people, to themselves and to all of us, are the uneducated people."
10134{_}1044{_}"Yes, I remember," J.W.
10134{_}1045{_}admitted.
10134{_}1046{_}"'Cultural and social values of education,' he called that, didn't he?
10134{_}1047{_}And that's what I'm not sure of.
10134{_}1048{_}It seems pretty foggy to me.
10134{_}1049{_}But, old man, you're going, that's settled, and maybe I'll just let dad send me to keep you company, if I can't find any better reason."
10134{_}1050{_}"That's all very well for you to say, J.W.," Marty retorted, with the least little touch of resentment in his tone.
10134{_}1051{_}"You'll _let_ your dad send you.
10134{_}1052{_}My dad can't send me, though he'll do all he's able to do, and how I can earn enough, to get through is more than I can see from here."
10134{_}1053{_}But J.W.
10134{_}1054{_}asserted, confidently: "There's a way, just the same, and I think I know how to find out about it.
10134{_}1055{_}I haven't been a second assistant deputy secretary in the Sunday school for nothing.
10134{_}1056{_}You reminded me of the commencement address; I'll ask you if you remember Children's Day?
10134{_}1057{_}It came the very next Sunday."
10134{_}1058{_}"Yes, I remember it; but what of it?"
10134{_}1059{_}"Well, my boy, we took up a collection for you!"
10134{_}1060{_}"We did?
10134{_}1061{_}Not much we did, and anyway, do you think I'd accept that sort of help?
10134{_}1062{_}I'm not looking for charity, yet," and Marty showed the hurt he felt.
10134{_}1063{_}"Steady, Martin Luther!
10134{_}1064{_}I wouldn't want you to get that collection anyway; it wasn't near big enough.
10134{_}1065{_}But don't you know that every Children's Day collection in the whole church goes to the Board of Education, and that it has become a big fund, never to be given away but always to be loaned to students getting ready to be preachers and such?
10134{_}1066{_}It's no charity; it's the same broad-minded business you want me to go to college for.
10134{_}1067{_}I can see that much without getting any nearer to college than the Delafield First Church Sunday School.
10134{_}1068{_}You borrow the money, just as if you stepped up to a bank window, and you agree to pay it back as soon as you can after you graduate.
10134{_}1069{_}Then it goes into the Fund again, and some other boy or girl borrows it, and so on.
10134{_}1070{_}More than twenty-five thousand students have borrowed from this fund.
10134{_}1071{_}About fifteen hundred of 'em got loans last year.
10134{_}1072{_}Ask the preacher if I'm not giving you this straight."
10134{_}1073{_}Marty had no immediate way of testing this unusual wealth of information, so he said, "Well, maybe there's something in it.
10134{_}1074{_}I'll talk to Brother Drury about it, anyway."
10134{_}1075{_}That observing man was quite willing to be talked to.
10134{_}1076{_}When Marty presented himself at the study a few days later he found the pastor as well prepared as if he had been expecting some such interview, as, indeed, he had.
10134{_}1077{_}He told Marty the story of the Student Loan Fund--how it originated in the celebration of the Centenary of American Methodism, in 1866, and how it had been growing all through the years, both by the annual Children's Day offering and by the increasing return of loans from former students.
10134{_}1078{_}Then he explained that this Fund, and many other educational affairs, were in the hands of the Church's Board of Education.
10134{_}1079{_}This Board, Marty heard, is a sort of educational clearing house for the whole church, and especially for Methodist schools of higher learning.
10134{_}1080{_}It helps young people to go to college, and it helps the colleges to take care of the young people when they go, of course always using money which has come from the churches.
10134{_}1081{_}It has charge of a group of special schools in the South, and it sets the scholastic standards to which all the church's schools and colleges must conform.
10134{_}1082{_}Besides looking out for these interests it helps the school to provide courses in the Bible and Christian principles, and it furnishes workers to serve the colleges in caring for the religious life of the students.
10134{_}1083{_}Marty listened carefully, and with no lack of interest, but when the minister paused the boy's mind sprang back to his own particular concern.
10134{_}1084{_}"But, Mr. Drury, can any student borrow money from that fund?"
10134{_}1085{_}"Well, no," said the preacher, "not every student.
10134{_}1086{_}Only those who are preparing for the ministry or for other careers of special service.
10134{_}1087{_}They have to show that the loan will help them in preparing to be of some definite Christian value when they graduate.
10134{_}1088{_}That won't affect you; you can borrow, not all you could use, perhaps, but enough to be a big help.
10134{_}1089{_}How much do you expect to need?"
10134{_}1090{_}"Why," answered Marty, "I hardly know.
10134{_}1091{_}I hadn't really thought it possible I could go.
10134{_}1092{_}But dad says he'll let me have all he can, and they tell me a fellow can get work to do if he's not particular about easy jobs.
10134{_}1093{_}I'm pretty sure I could manage, except for tuition and books, but----"  "Then you may as well consider it settled," said the pastor, "Cartwright College will welcome you on those terms, or I'll know the reason why.
10134{_}1094{_}And I think you can count on J.W.
10134{_}1095{_}going with you."
10134{_}1096{_}J.W.
10134{_}1097{_}was not hard to convince.
10134{_}1098{_}His parents were all for it.
10134{_}1099{_}The pastor had no intention of overdoing his own part in the affair, and contented himself with a suggestion that disposed of J.W.
10134{_}1100{_}'s main objection.
10134{_}1101{_}J.W.
10134{_}1102{_}had been saying to him one day, "I know I should have a good time at college, but I should be four years later getting into business than the other boys."
10134{_}1103{_}"That depends on what 'later' means," replied Mr. Drury.
10134{_}1104{_}"You would not need four years to catch up, if college does for you what I think it will.
10134{_}1105{_}Besides, you're intending to be a Christian citizen, I take it, and that will be even more of a job than to be a successful hardware man.
10134{_}1106{_}Colleges have been operating these many years, to give young people the best possible preparations for a whole life.
10134{_}1107{_}Remember what John Milton said: I care not how late I come, so I come fit.'
10134{_}1108{_}You want to come to your work as fit as they make 'em, don't you?"
10134{_}1109{_}And J.W.
10134{_}1110{_}owned up that he did.
10134{_}1111{_}"I don't mean to be a dub in business, and I've no right to be a dub anywhere.
10134{_}1112{_}Me for Cartwright, Brother Drury!"
10134{_}1113{_}Another day's work in the laboratory.
10134{_}1114{_}Walter Drury knew how to be patient, yet every experience like this was a tonic to his soul.
10134{_}1115{_}And now he must be content for a time to let others carry the work through its next stages, though he would hold himself ready for any unexpected development that might arise.
10134{_}1116{_}So it befell that J.W.
10134{_}1117{_}and Marty started to Cartwright, and a week later Joe Carbrook went off to the State University.
10134{_}1118{_}The day after they had matriculated, J.W.
10134{_}1119{_}and Marty were putting their room to rights--oh, yes, they thought it would be well to share the same room--and as they puttered about they reviewed the happenings of the first day.
10134{_}1120{_}They had made a preliminary exploration of the grounds and buildings, revisiting the places which had become familiar during Institute week, and living over that crowded and epochal time.
10134{_}1121{_}Marty, scouting around for something to do, had discovered that he could get work, such as it was, for ten hours a week, anyway, and maybe more, at thirty to fifty cents an hour.
10134{_}1122{_}He had a little money left after paying his tuition, and the college registrar assured him that the loan from the Board of Education would be forthcoming.
10134{_}1123{_}Therefore the talk turned on money.
10134{_}1124{_}"That tuition bill sure reduced the swelling in my pocketbook, Marty," remarked J.W., as he examined his visible resources.
10134{_}1125{_}"What do you think it did to mine?"
10134{_}1126{_}Marty observed quietly.
10134{_}1127{_}"I'm still giddy from being relieved of so much money in one operation.
10134{_}1128{_}And yet I can't see how they get along.
10134{_}1129{_}Look at the big faculty they have, and all these buildings to keep up and keep going.
10134{_}1130{_}When I think of how big a dollar seems to me, the tuition looks like the national debt of Mexico; but when I try to figure out how much it costs the college per student, I feel as though I were paying lunch-counter prices for a dining-car dinner.
10134{_}1131{_}How _do_ they do it, J.W.?"
10134{_}1132{_}"Who told you I was to be looked on in the light of a World Almanac, my son?
10134{_}1133{_}I could give you the answer to that question without getting out of my chair, but for one small difficulty--I just don't know.
10134{_}1134{_}Tell you what--it's a good question--let's look in the catalogue.
10134{_}1135{_}I'd like to find information in that volume about something besides the four centuries of study that loom before my freshman eyes."
10134{_}1136{_}So they looked in the catalogue and discovered that Cartwright College had an endowment of $1,750,000, producing an income of about $80,000 a year, and that the churches of its territory gave about $25,000 more.
10134{_}1137{_}They learned also that most of the buildings had been provided by friends of the college, with the Carnegie Library mainly the gift of the millionaire ironmaster.
10134{_}1138{_}They learned also that about $500,000 of the endowment had been raised in the last two years, under the promise of the General Education Board, which is a Rockefeller creation, to provide the last $125,000.
10134{_}1139{_}The college property was valued at about half a million dollars.
10134{_}1140{_}"And there you are, Martin Luther, my bold reformer," said J.W., cheerfully.
10134{_}1141{_}"The people who put up the money have invested about two and a half millions on you and me, and the other five hundred students, say about $250 a year per student.
10134{_}1142{_}And we pay the rest of what it costs to give us a college career, $125 to $175 a year, depending on our taste in courses.
10134{_}1143{_}I remember I felt as if the John Wesley Farwell family had almost gone broke when dad signed up for $1,000 on that last endowment campaign.
10134{_}1144{_}I thought the money gone forever, but I see now he merely invested it.
10134{_}1145{_}I've come to Cartwright to spend the income of it, and a little more.
10134{_}1146{_}Five or six people have given a thousand dollars apiece to make a college course possible for each of us.
10134{_}1147{_}There's some reason in college endowments, after all."
10134{_}1148{_}And Marty said, "One good I can see in this particular endowment is that anybody but a selfish idiot would be glad to match four years of his life against all the money and work that Christian people have put into Cartwright College."
10134{_}1149{_}"I hope you don't mean anything personal by that remark," J.W.
10134{_}1150{_}said, with mock solemnity, "because I'm inclined to believe you're more than half right.
10134{_}1151{_}It reminds me again of what Phil Khamis said.
10134{_}1152{_}I'm beginning to think I'll never have a chance to forget that Greek's Christian remark about Christians."
10134{_}1153{_}By being off at school together J.W.
10134{_}1154{_}and Marty gave each other unconfessed but very real moral support in those first days when a lone freshman would have known he was homesick.
10134{_}1155{_}But another antidote, both pleasant and potent, was supplied by the Epworth League of First Church.
10134{_}1156{_}It had allied itself with the college Y.M.C.A.--and for the women students, with the Y.W.C.A.--in various ways, but particularly it purposed to see that the first few Sundays were safely tided over.
10134{_}1157{_}So the two chums found themselves in one of the two highly attractive study courses which had been put on in partnership with the Sunday school.
10134{_}1158{_}It was in the early afternoon of one of the early Sundays that J.W.
10134{_}1159{_}called Marty's attention to a still more alluring opportunity.
10134{_}1160{_}"Looky here, Marty, it's raining, I know, but I've a feeling that you'd better not write that letter home until a little further on in the day.
10134{_}1161{_}What's to stop us from taking a look at this League fellowship hour we're invited to, and getting a light lunch?
10134{_}1162{_}We don't need to stay to the League meeting unless we choose, though we're members, you know."
10134{_}1163{_}Marty picked up the card of invitation which J.W.
10134{_}1164{_}had flipped across the table to him, and read it.
10134{_}1165{_}"Well," he commented, "it reads all right.
10134{_}1166{_}Let's try it."
10134{_}1167{_}Out into the rain they went and put in two highly cheerful hours, including one in the devotional meeting, so that when Marty at last sat down to write home, he produced, without quite knowing how, a letter that was vastly more heartening when it reached the farm than it would have been if he had written it before dark.
10134{_}1168{_}Joe Carbrook set out for the State University in what was for him a fashion quite subdued.
10134{_}1169{_}Before his experience at the Institute he would have gone, if at all, in his own car, and his arrival would have been notice to "the sporty crowd" that another candidate for initiation into that select circle had arrived.
10134{_}1170{_}But Joe was enjoying the novelty of thinking a little before he acted.
10134{_}1171{_}Though he would always be of the irrepressible sort, he was not the same Joe.
10134{_}1172{_}He had laid out a program which surprised himself somewhat, and astonished most of the people who knew him.
10134{_}1173{_}He knew now that he would become, if he could, a doctor; a missionary doctor.
10134{_}1174{_}No other career entered his mind.
10134{_}1175{_}He would finish his college work at the State University, and then go to medical school.
10134{_}1176{_}He would devote himself without ceasing to all the studies he would need.
10134{_}1177{_}Not for him any social life, any relaxation of purpose.
10134{_}1178{_}Grimly he told himself that his play days were over.
10134{_}1179{_}They had been lively while they lasted; but they were done.
10134{_}1180{_}Of course that was foolish.
10134{_}1181{_}If he had persisted in any such scholastic regimen, the effort would have lasted a few days, or possibly weeks; and then in a reaction of disgust he might easily have come to despair of the whole project.
10134{_}1182{_}Fortunately for Joe and for a good many other people, his purpose of digging into his books and laboratory work and doggedly avoiding any other interest was tempered by the happenings of the first week.
10134{_}1183{_}Doubtless he would have made a desperate struggle, but it would have been useless.
10134{_}1184{_}Not even conversion can make new habits overnight, and in his first two years at college Joe had been known to teachers and students alike as distinctly a sketchy student, wholly inexpert at concentrated effort.
10134{_}1185{_}And so, instead of becoming first a grind and then a discouraged rebel against it all, he had the immense good fortune to be captured by an observant Junior whom he had met while they were both registering for Chemistry III.
10134{_}1186{_}"You're new here," said the Junior, Heatherby by name, "and I've had two years of it.
10134{_}1187{_}Maybe you'll let me show you the place.
10134{_}1188{_}I'm the proud half-owner of a decidedly second-hand 'Hooting Nanny,' you know, and I rather like bumping people around town in it."
10134{_}1189{_}That was the beginning of many things.
10134{_}1190{_}Joe liked it that Heatherby made no apologies for his car, and before long he discovered that the other half-owner, Barnard, was equally unaffected and friendly.
10134{_}1191{_}It was something of a surprise, though, to learn that Barnard was not a student, but the youthful-looking pastor of the University Methodist Church, of late known as the Wesley Foundation.
10134{_}1192{_}"I'm not up on Methodism as I should be," said Joe to Barnard, a day or two later, "and I may as well admit that I never heard before of this Wesley Foundation of yours.
10134{_}1193{_}Is it a church affair?"
10134{_}1194{_}"Well, rather," Barnard answered.
10134{_}1195{_}"It is just exactly that.
10134{_}1196{_}You know, or could have guessed, that a good many of the students here are from Methodist homes--about a fourth of the whole student body, as it happens.
10134{_}1197{_}And our church has been coming to see, perhaps a bit slowly, that although the State could not provide any religious influences, and could certainly do nothing for denominational interests, there was all the more reason for the church to do it.
10134{_}1198{_}That's the idea under the Foundation, so to speak, and the work is now established in nine of the great State Universities."
10134{_}1199{_}"Yes, I see," Joe mused, "but just what is the Foundation's duty, and how do you do it?"
10134{_}1200{_}Barnard laughed as he said, "We do pretty near everything, in this University.
10134{_}1201{_}We have a regular Methodist church, with a membership made up almost entirely of faculty and students.
10134{_}1202{_}The town people have their own First Church, over on the West Side.
10134{_}1203{_}Our church has its Sunday school, its Epworth League Chapter, and other activities.
10134{_}1204{_}We try to come out strong on the social side, and in a little while, when our Social Center building is up--we're after the money for it now--we can do a good deal more.
10134{_}1205{_}There is plenty of demand for it."
10134{_}1206{_}"That's all church work, of course.
10134{_}1207{_}I suppose you have no relation to the University, though," Joe asked, "studies and all that?"
10134{_}1208{_}"Yes, indeed, and we're coming to more of it, but gradually.
10134{_}1209{_}We are already offering courses in religious subjects, with teachers recognized by the University, and credit given.
10134{_}1210{_}It's all very new yet, you know, but we're hoping and going ahead."
10134{_}1211{_}"I should think so," said Joe with emphasis.
10134{_}1212{_}"But where does the money come from for all this?
10134{_}1213{_}It must be Methodist money, of course; who puts it up?"
10134{_}1214{_}"Oh, the usual people," said Barnard.
10134{_}1215{_}"A few well-to-do Methodists have provided some of it, but the really big money has to come from the churches--collections and subscriptions and all that.
10134{_}1216{_}This sort of work is being done in forty-odd other schools, where the Wesley Foundation is not organized.
10134{_}1217{_}The money comes officially through two of the benevolent boards."
10134{_}1218{_}"Yes?"
10134{_}1219{_}queried Joe.
10134{_}1220{_}"I've often heard of 'the benevolences,' but I never thought of them as meaning anything to me.
10134{_}1221{_}How do they hook up to a proposition like that?"
10134{_}1222{_}"Well," said Barnard, "the Board of Education, naturally, is interested because of the Methodist students who are here.
10134{_}1223{_}And the Board of Home Missions and Church Extension is interested because at bottom this is the realest sort of home mission and church extension work."
10134{_}1224{_}"Do these boards supply all the money you need?"
10134{_}1225{_}was Joe's next question.
10134{_}1226{_}"No, not all at once, anyway," Barnard answered.
10134{_}1227{_}"We're needing a good deal more before this thing really gets on its feet; and when our people know what work can be done in State schools, and what a glorious chance we have, I think they'll see that the money is provided.
10134{_}1228{_}The students are there, half a hundred thousand of them, and the church must be there too."
10134{_}1229{_}"Well," Joe said, "I admire the faith of you.
10134{_}1230{_}And I want to join.
10134{_}1231{_}You know, although I'm a mighty green hand at religious work, I've got to go at it hard.
10134{_}1232{_}There's a reason.
10134{_}1233{_}So please count me in on everything where I'm likely to fit at all.
10134{_}1234{_}I didn't tell you, did I, that I'm headed for medicine?--going to be a missionary doctor, if they'll take me when I'm ready.
10134{_}1235{_}Maybe your Foundation can do something with me."
10134{_}1236{_}Barnard thought it could, and the next two years justified his confidence.
10134{_}1237{_}Joe Carbrook, as downright in his new purpose as he had been in his old scornful refusal to look at life seriously, quickly found a place for himself in the church and the other activities of the Foundation.
10134{_}1238{_}It saved him from his first heedless resolution to study an impossible number of hours a day, and from the certain crash which would have followed.
10134{_}1239{_}It gave him not a few friends, and he was soon deep in the affairs of the League and the church.
10134{_}1240{_}Besides, it made possible some special friendships among the faculty, which were to be of immense value in later days.
10134{_}1241{_}While Joe Carbrook was fitting himself into the life of the University and the Wesley Foundation, the chums at Cartwright were quite as busy making themselves a part of their new world.
10134{_}1242{_}As always, they made a good team, so much so that people began to think of them not as individuals, but as necessarily related, like a pair of shoes, or collar and tie, or pork and beans.
10134{_}1243{_}And, though the old differences of temperament and interest had not lessened, the two had reached a fine contentment over each other's purposes.
10134{_}1244{_}J.W.
10134{_}1245{_}was happy in Marty's preacher-plans, and Marty believed implicitly in the wisdom of J.W.
10134{_}1246{_}'s understood purpose to be a forthright Christian layman.
10134{_}1247{_}But it was not all plain sailing for J.W.
10134{_}1248{_}Nobody bothered Marty; he was going into the ministry, and that settled that.
10134{_}1249{_}Among the students who went in for religious work were several who could not quite share Marty's complacence over J.W.
10134{_}1250{_}'s program.
10134{_}1251{_}They thought it strange that so active a Christian, with the right stuff in him, as everybody recognized, should not declare himself for some religious vocation.
10134{_}1252{_}And from time to time men came to college--bishops, secretaries, specialists--to talk to the students about this very thing.
10134{_}1253{_}There was a student volunteer band, in which were enrolled all the students looking to foreign mission work.
10134{_}1254{_}The prospective preachers had a club of their own, and there was even a little organized group of boys and girls who thought seriously of social service in some form or another as a career.
10134{_}1255{_}Now, J.W., before the end of sophomore year, had come to know all, or nearly all, of these young enthusiasts.
10134{_}1256{_}Some of them developed into staunch and satisfying friends.
10134{_}1257{_}If he had run with the sport crowd, which was always looking for recruits, or if he had been merely a hard student, working for Phi Beta Kappa, he might have been let alone.
10134{_}1258{_}But, without being able to wear an identifying label, he yet belonged with those who had come to college with a definite life purpose.
10134{_}1259{_}Just because nobody seemed to realize that being a Christian in business could be as distinct a vocation as any, J.W.
10134{_}1260{_}was at times vaguely troubled, in spite of his confident stand at the Institute.
10134{_}1261{_}He wondered a little at what he had almost come to feel was his callousness.
10134{_}1262{_}Not that he was uninterested; for Marty he had vast unspoken ambitions which would have stunned that unsuspecting youth if they had ever become vocal; and he never tired of the prospects which opened up before his other friends.
10134{_}1263{_}He kept up an intermittent correspondence with Joe Carbrook, and found himself thinking much about the strange chain of circumstances which promised to make a medical missionary out of Joe.
10134{_}1264{_}He more than suspected that Joe and Marcia Dayne were vastly interested in each other's future, and he got a lot of satisfaction out of that.
10134{_}1265{_}They would have a great missionary career.
10134{_}1266{_}No; he was not unfeeling about all these high purposes of the boys and girls he knew; and if he could just get a final answer to the one question that was bothering him, his college life would need nothing to make it wholly satisfying.
10134{_}1267{_}He had early forgotten all his old reluctance to put college before business.
10134{_}1268{_}Marty knew something of what was passing in J.W.
10134{_}1269{_}'s mind, and it troubled him a little.
10134{_}1270{_}He thought of tackling J.W.
10134{_}1271{_}himself, and by this time there was nothing under the sun they could not discuss with each other freely.
10134{_}1272{_}But he did not quite trust himself.
10134{_}1273{_}At last he made up his mind to write to their pastor at home.
10134{_}1274{_}He knew that for some reason Mr. Drury had a peculiar interest in J.W.
10134{_}1275{_}and was sure he could count on it now.
10134{_}1276{_}"I know J.W.
10134{_}1277{_}'s bothered," he wrote, "but he doesn't talk about it.
10134{_}1278{_}I think he has been disturbed by hearing so much about special calls to special work.
10134{_}1279{_}We've had several lifework meetings lately, and the needs of the world have been pretty strongly stated.
10134{_}1280{_}But the stand he took at the Institute is just as right for him as mine is for me.
10134{_}1281{_}Can't you write to him, or something?"
10134{_}1282{_}Walter Drury could do better than write.
10134{_}1283{_}He turned up at Cartwright that same week.
10134{_}1284{_}It happened that three or four prospective preachers and Christian workers had been in their room that afternoon, and J.W.
10134{_}1285{_}was trying to think the thing through once more.
10134{_}1286{_}He recalled what his pastor had said at the camp fire, and his own testimony on Institute Sunday in the life-service meeting, after Marcia Dayne had put it up to him.
10134{_}1287{_}But he was making heavy weather of it.
10134{_}1288{_}And just then came the pastor's knock at the door.
10134{_}1289{_}There was a boisterous welcome from them both, with something like relief in J.W.
10134{_}1290{_}'s heart, that he would not, could not speak.
10134{_}1291{_}But he could get help now.
10134{_}1292{_}For the sake of saying something he asked the usual question.
10134{_}1293{_}"What in the world brings you to Cartwright?"
10134{_}1294{_}"Oh," said Pastor Drury, "I like to come to Cartwright.
10134{_}1295{_}Your President's an old friend.
10134{_}1296{_}Besides, why shouldn't I come to see you two, if I wish?
10134{_}1297{_}You are still part of my flock, you know."
10134{_}1298{_}So they talked of anything and everything.
10134{_}1299{_}By and by Marty said he must go over to the library, and pretty soon J.W.
10134{_}1300{_}was telling his friend the pastor all that had been disturbing him.
10134{_}1301{_}"It all began in the summer before I came to college, at the Institute here, you know, when you spoke at the camp fire on Saturday night."
10134{_}1302{_}"I remember," the pastor replied.
10134{_}1303{_}"You hadn't taken much interest in your future work before that?"
10134{_}1304{_}"No real interest, I guess," J.W.
10134{_}1305{_}admitted.
10134{_}1306{_}"I'd always taken things as they came, and didn't go looking for what I couldn't see.
10134{_}1307{_}I was enjoying every day's living, and didn't care deeply about anything else.
10134{_}1308{_}Why, though I've been a Methodist all my life, you remember how I knew nothing at all about the Methodist Church outside of Delafield, except what little I picked up about its Sunday schools by serving as an assistant to our Sunday school secretary.
10134{_}1309{_}And when I began to hear, at the Institute, about home missions and foreign missions, about Negro education and other business that the church was doing, I saw right off that it was up to us young people to supply the new workers that were always needed.
10134{_}1310{_}But, even so, only those who had a real fitness for it ought to offer themselves, and I thought too that something else would be needed.
10134{_}1311{_}I wasn't any duller than lots of other church members--even the older ones didn't seem to know much more about the church outside than I did.
10134{_}1312{_}You would take up collections for the benevolences, but if you told us what they meant, we didn't pay enough attention to get the idea clearly, so as to have any real understanding.
10134{_}1313{_}I suppose the women's societies had more.
10134{_}1314{_}I know my mother talks about Industrial Homes in the South, and schools in India--she's in both the societies, you know--but that is about all."
10134{_}1315{_}"And it seemed when I began to find out about things, Mr. Drury, that if our whole church needed workers for all these places, it needed just as much to have in the local churches men and women who would know about the work in a big way, and who would care in a big way, to back up the whole work as it should be backed up.
10134{_}1316{_}So, when you spoke at the camp fire it was just what I wanted to hear, and when I was called on, I made that sort of a declaration the next day at the life decision services."
10134{_}1317{_}"Yes I remember that too," said Mr. Drury, "and I remember telling Joe Carbrook that you had undertaken as big a career as any of them."
10134{_}1318{_}"That's what I kind of thought too," said J.W., simply, "but rooming with Marty Shenk--he's going to make a great preacher too--keeps me thinking, and I know about all the students who are getting ready for special work, and lately I've been wondering----"  "About some special sort of work you'd like to do?"
10134{_}1319{_}Mr. Drury prompted.
10134{_}1320{_}"No; not that at all.
10134{_}1321{_}I'm just as sure as ever I'm not that sort.
10134{_}1322{_}If only I can make good in business, there's where I belong.
10134{_}1323{_}But can a fellow make good just as a Christian in the same way I expect Marty Shenk to make good as a Christian preacher?"
10134{_}1324{_}The pastor stood up and came over to J.W.
10134{_}1325{_}'s chair.
10134{_}1326{_}"My boy, I know just what you are facing.
10134{_}1327{_}It is a pretty old struggle, and there's only one way out of it.
10134{_}1328{_}God hasn't any first place and second place for the people that let him guide them.
10134{_}1329{_}A man may refuse his call, either to go or to stay, and then no matter what he does it will be a second best.
10134{_}1330{_}But you--wait for your call.
10134{_}1331{_}For my part, I think probably you've got it, and it's to a very real life.
10134{_}1332{_}If you and those like you should fail, we should soon have no more missionaries.
10134{_}1333{_}And if the missionaries should fail, we should soon have no more church.
10134{_}1334{_}God has little patience with a church that always stays at home, and I doubt if he has more for a church that doesn't stand by the men and women it has sent to the outposts.
10134{_}1335{_}It is all one job."
10134{_}1336{_}There was much more of the same sort, and when J.W.
10134{_}1337{_}walked with his pastor to the train the next morning, the only doubt that had ever really disturbed him in college was quieted for good.
10134{_}1338{_}Walter Drury went back to Delafield and his work, surer now than ever that the Experiment was going forward.
10134{_}1339{_}He knew, certainly, that all this was only the getting ready; that the real tests would come later But he was well content.
10134{_}1340{_}*       *       *       *       *  It was early football season of the junior year.
10134{_}1341{_}The State University took on Cartwright College for the first Saturday's game, everybody well knowing that it was only a practice romp for the University.
10134{_}1342{_}Always a big time for Cartwright, this year it was a day for remembering.
10134{_}1343{_}Joe Carbrook, who had been graduated from the University in June, and was now a medical student in the city, drove down to see the game.
10134{_}1344{_}For loyalty's sake he joined the little bunch of University rooters on the east stand.
10134{_}1345{_}Otherwise it was Cartwright's crowd, as well as Cartwright's day.
10134{_}1346{_}To the surprise of everybody, neither side scored until the last quarter, and then both sides made a touchdown, Cartwright first!
10134{_}1347{_}A high tricky wind spoiled both attempts to kick goal, and time was called with a score at 6-6.
10134{_}1348{_}Cartwright had held State to a tie, for the first time in history!
10134{_}1349{_}Joe came from the game with the chums and took supper with them.
10134{_}1350{_}The whole town was ablaze with excitement over its team's great showing against the State, and the talk at table was all of the way Cartwright's eleven could now go romping down the schedule and take every other college into camp, including, of course, Barton Poly, their dearest foe.
10134{_}1351{_}The boys were happy to have Joe with them, he looked so big and fine, and had the same easy, breezy bearing as of old.
10134{_}1352{_}Nor had he lost any of that frank attitude toward his own career which never failed to interest everybody he met.
10134{_}1353{_}After supper they had an hour together in the room.
10134{_}1354{_}"Those boys in the medical school surely do amuse me," he laughed.
10134{_}1355{_}"When I tell 'em I'm to be a missionary doctor, which I do first thing to give 'em sort of a shock they don't often get, they stand off and say, 'What, you!'
10134{_}1356{_}as if I had told 'em I was to be a traffic cop, or a trapeze artist in the circus.
10134{_}1357{_}Some of 'em seem to think I'm queer in the head, but, boys, they are the ones with rooms to let.
10134{_}1358{_}When the others talk about hanging out a shingle in Chicago or Saint Louis or Cleveland or some other over-doctored place, I tell 'em to watch me, when I'm the only doctor between Siam and sunrise!
10134{_}1359{_}Won't I be somebody?
10134{_}1360{_}With my own hospital--made out o' mud, I know--and a dispensary and a few native helpers who don't know what I'm going to do next, and all the sick people coming from ten days' journey away to the foreign doctor!"
10134{_}1361{_}And then his mood changed.
10134{_}1362{_}"That's what'll get me, though; all those helpless, ignorant humans who don't even know what I can do for their bodies, let alone having any suspicion of what Somebody Else can do for their souls!
10134{_}1363{_}But it will be wonderful; next thing to being with him in Galilee!"
10134{_}1364{_}There was a pause, each boy filling it with thoughts he would not speak.
10134{_}1365{_}"Where do you expect to find that work, Joe?"
10134{_}1366{_}J.W.
10134{_}1367{_}asked him.
10134{_}1368{_}The answer was quick and straight: "Wherever I'm sent, J.W., boy," he said.
10134{_}1369{_}"Only I've told the candidate secretary what I want.
10134{_}1370{_}I met him last summer in Chicago, and there's nothing like getting in your bid early.
10134{_}1371{_}He's agreed to recommend me, when I'm ready, for the hardest, neediest, most neglected place that's open.
10134{_}1372{_}If I'm going into this missionary doctor business, I want a chance to prove Christianity where they won't be able to say that Christianity couldn't have done it alone.
10134{_}1373{_}It _can_!"
10134{_}1374{_}Then, with one of those quick turns which were Joe Carbrook's devices for concealing his feelings, he said, "And how's everything going at this Methodist college of yours?
10134{_}1375{_}Your boys put up a beautiful game to-day, and they ought to have won.
10134{_}1376{_}How's the rest of the school?"
10134{_}1377{_}Both the boys assured him everything was going in a properly satisfactory fashion, but Marty had caught one word that he wanted Joe to enlarge upon.
10134{_}1378{_}"Why do you say 'Methodist college'?
10134{_}1379{_}It is a Methodist college; but is there anything the matter with that?"
10134{_}1380{_}Joe rose to the mild challenge.
10134{_}1381{_}"Don't think I mean to be nasty," he said, "but I can't help comparing this place with the State University, and I wonder if there's any big reason for such colleges as this.
10134{_}1382{_}You know they all have a hard time, and the State spends dollars to the church's dimes."
10134{_}1383{_}"Yes, we know that, don't we, J.W.?"
10134{_}1384{_}and Marty appealed to his chum, remembering the frequent and half-curious talks they had on that very contrast.
10134{_}1385{_}J.W.
10134{_}1386{_}said "Sure," but plainly meant to leave the defense of the Christian college to Marty, who, to tell the truth, was quite willing.
10134{_}1387{_}"There's room for both, and need for both," said that earnest young man.
10134{_}1388{_}"Each has its work to do--the State University will probably help in attracting most of those who want special technical equipment, and the church colleges will keep on serving those who want an education for its own sake, whatever special line they may take up afterward: though each will say it welcomes both sorts of students."
10134{_}1389{_}This suited Joe; he intended Marty to keep it up a while.
10134{_}1390{_}So he said, "But why is a church college, anyway?"
10134{_}1391{_}And he got his answer, for Marty too was eager for the fray.
10134{_}1392{_}"The church college," he retorted with the merest hint of asperity, "is at the bottom of all that people call higher education.
10134{_}1393{_}The church was founding colleges and supporting them before the State thought even of primary schools.
10134{_}1394{_}Look at Oxford and Cambridge--church colleges.
10134{_}1395{_}Look at Harvard and Yale and Princeton and the smaller New England colleges--church colleges.
10134{_}1396{_}Look at Syracuse and Wesleyan and Northwestern and Chicago.
10134{_}1397{_}Look at Vanderbilt, and most of the other great schools of the South.
10134{_}1398{_}They are church colleges, founded, most of them, before the first State University, and many before there was any public high school.
10134{_}1399{_}The church college showed the way.
10134{_}1400{_}If it had never done anything else, it has some rights as the pioneer of higher learning."
10134{_}1401{_}J.W.
10134{_}1402{_}had been getting more interested.
10134{_}1403{_}He had never heard Marty in quite this strain, and he was proud of him.
10134{_}1404{_}"That's a pretty good answer he's given you, Joe," he said with a chuckle.
10134{_}1405{_}"Now, isn't it?"
10134{_}1406{_}"It is," admitted Joe.
10134{_}1407{_}"I reckon I knew most of what you say, Marty, but I hadn't thought of it that way before.
10134{_}1408{_}Now I want to ask another question, only don't think I'm doing it for meanness; I've got a reason.
10134{_}1409{_}And my question is this: granting all that the church schools have done, is it worth all they cost to keep them up now; in our time, I mean?"
10134{_}1410{_}"I think it is," Marty answered, quieter now.
10134{_}1411{_}"They do provide a different sort of educational opportunity, as I said.
10134{_}1412{_}Then, they are producing most of the recruits that the churches need for their work.
10134{_}1413{_}Since the churches began to care for their members in the State Universities, a rather larger number of candidates for Christian service are coming out of the universities, but until the last year or two nearly all came, and the very large majority still comes, and probably for years will come, from the church colleges.
10134{_}1414{_}And there's another reason that you State advocates ought to remember.
10134{_}1415{_}Our Methodist colleges in this country have about fifty thousand students.
10134{_}1416{_}If these colleges were to be put out of business, ten of the very greatest State Universities would have to be duplicated, dollar for dollar, at public expense, to take care of the Methodist students alone.
10134{_}1417{_}When you think of all the other denominations, you would need to duplicate all the State Universities now in existence if you purposed to do the work the church colleges are now doing.
10134{_}1418{_}And if you couldn't get the money, or if the students didn't take to the change, the country would be short just that many thousand college-trained men and women.
10134{_}1419{_}The whole Methodist Church, with the other churches, is doing a piece of unselfish national service that costs up into the hundreds of millions, and where's any other big money that's better spent?"
10134{_}1420{_}When Marty stopped he looked up into Joe's good-natured face, and blushed, with an embarrassed self-consciousness.
10134{_}1421{_}"You think you've been stringing me, don't you?"
10134{_}1422{_}"Now, Marty," Joe spoke genially, "don't you misunderstand.
10134{_}1423{_}I said I had a reason.
10134{_}1424{_}I have.
10134{_}1425{_}My folks have some money they want to put into a safe place.
10134{_}1426{_}And they like Cartwright.
10134{_}1427{_}I do too, but--you know how it is.
10134{_}1428{_}I want to be sure.
10134{_}1429{_}Anyhow I'm glad I asked these questions.
10134{_}1430{_}You've given me some highly important information; and, honestly, I'm grateful.
10134{_}1431{_}You surely don't think I'm small enough to be making fun of you, or of Cartwright.
10134{_}1432{_}If I seemed to be, I apologize on the spot.
10134{_}1433{_}Believe me?"
10134{_}1434{_}and there was no mistaking his genuine earnestness.
10134{_}1435{_}"Of course I believe you, old man," Marty rejoined, just a wee bit ashamed.
10134{_}1436{_}"Forgive me too, but I've been reading up on that college thing lately, and it's a little different from what most people think.
10134{_}1437{_}So you got me going."
10134{_}1438{_}"I'm glad he did," said J.W.
10134{_}1439{_}"It makes me prouder than ever of Cartwright College."
10134{_}1440{_}And, as he got up he said, as though still at the game, "The 'locomotive' now!"
10134{_}1441{_}and gave Cartwright's favorite yell as a solo, while Marty and Joe grinned approval and some students passing in the street answered it with the "skyrocket."
10134{_}1442{_}*       *       *       *       *  There is material for a book, all mixt of interest varying from very light comedy to unplumbed gloom, in the life of two boys at college--any two; and some day the chronicles of the Delafield Duo may be written; but not now.
10134{_}1443{_}Senior year, with its bright glory and its seriously borne responsibilities.
10134{_}1444{_}It found Marty a trifle less shy and reticent than when he came to Cartwright, and J.W., Jr., a shade more studious.
10134{_}1445{_}Marty would miss Phi Beta Kappa, but only by the merest fraction; J.W.
10134{_}1446{_}would rank about number twenty-seven in a graduating class of forty-five.
10134{_}1447{_}Marty had successfully represented his college twice in debate, and J.W.
10134{_}1448{_}had played second on the nine and end in the eleven, doing each job better than well, but rarely drawing the spotlight his way.
10134{_}1449{_}Curiously enough, you had but to talk to Marty, and you would learn that J.W., Jr., was the finest athlete and the most popular student in school.
10134{_}1450{_}Conversely, J.W., Jr., was prepared to set Cartwright's debating record, as incarnated in Marty, against that of any other college in the State.
10134{_}1451{_}What was more, he cherished an unshakable confidence that the "Rev.
10134{_}1452{_}Martin Luther Shenk" would be one of the leading ministers of his Conference within five years.
10134{_}1453{_}And so they came to commencement, with the Shenk and the Farwell families, Pastor Drury, and Marcia Dayne in the throng of visitors.
10134{_}1454{_}Mr. Drury rarely missed commencements at Cartwright, and naturally he could not stay away this year.
10134{_}1455{_}The Farwells thought Marcia might like to see her old schoolmates graduate, and the boys had written her that they wanted somebody they could trot around during commencement week who might be trusted to join in the "I knew him when" chorus without being tempted to introduce devastating reminiscences.
10134{_}1456{_}And Marcia, being in love with life and youth, had been delighted to accept the combined invitation.
10134{_}1457{_}She was not at all in love with either of the boys, nor they with her.
10134{_}1458{_}They thought they knew where her heart had been given, and they counted Joe Carbrook a lucky man.
10134{_}1459{_}"Tell us, Marcia," said J.W., Jr., one afternoon, as the three of them were down by the lake, "how it happens you went to the training school instead of the normal school last year."
10134{_}1460{_}"That's just like a man," said Marcia.
10134{_}1461{_}"Here am I, your awed and admiring slave, brought on to adorn the crowning event of your scholastic career, and you don't even remember that I finished the normal school course in three years, and graduated a year ago!"
10134{_}1462{_}Marty rolled over on the sand in wordless glee.
10134{_}1463{_}"Aw, now, Marcia, why----" J.W., Jr., boggled, fairly caught, but soon recovering himself.
10134{_}1464{_}"You must have been ashamed of it, then.
10134{_}1465{_}I do remember something about your getting through, now you mention the fact, but why didn't I receive an invitation?
10134{_}1466{_}Answer me that, young lady!"
10134{_}1467{_}"Oh, we educators don't think commencement amounts to so much as all that.
10134{_}1468{_}With us, you know, life is real, life is earnest, and so forth.
10134{_}1469{_}But I'll tell you the truth, J.W.
10134{_}1470{_}I knew you couldn't come, either of you, and I was saving up a little on commencement expenses; so I left you--and a good many others--off the list.
